                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent advances in nanostructured carbon for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Huimin; Huang, Yongxin; Ming, Hai; Cao, Gaoping; Zhang, Wenfeng; Ming, Jun; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1604-1630</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted soaring attention lately as a promising alternative to Li ion batteries (LIBs), because of the vast availability of Na, its low price and similar physicochem. properties to Li.  In recent years, significant progress of Na ion battery anodes, which restricted the development of SIBs in the past decades, was achieved.  Extensive studies demonstrated that carbonaceous materials can become the most promising anode candidates for SIBs due to their low cost, high stability and electronic cond.  A variety of C nanomaterials, including carbon quantum dots (CQDs), C nanotubes (CNTs), C nanofibers (CNFs), C nanosheets, and graphene as well as graphite and amorphous C anodes for SIBs, are briefly reviewed in view of their different dimensions and graphitization degrees.  It also elaborates on research on carbonaceous material modification by doping with heteroatoms, designing various porous morphologies or compositing with org. or inorg. species.  Finally, some perspectives and directions on C design for SIBs are also proposed.  These comprehensive and in-depth discussions will provide an insight into the optimization of carbonaceous materials in SIB anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcOLCu3I74t7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0licY-j9VLnsng"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Quantum Dots and Their Derivative 3D Porous Carbon Frameworks for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Ultralong Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Hongshuai; Banks, Craig E.; Jing, Mingjun; Zhang, Yan; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7861-7866</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, the extremely simplified and productive synthesis procedure of CQDs and their deriv. 3D porous carbon frameworks are studied.  Furthermore, the corresponding mechanism of CQDs and 3D PCFs were explored.  In addn., the obtained 3D PCFs was first applied as anode material for sodium-ion batteries with ultralong cycle life and outstanding rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowvU05IziAmrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0licY-j9VLnsng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslens7vL&amp;md5=57890cf0fb3b84b8eb1e328215eea7ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201802218"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Flexible Sulfur-Enriched Nitrogen Doped Multichannel Hollow Carbon Nanofibers Film for High Performance Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1802218</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-Doped Carbon Nanofibers with Interweaved Nanochannels for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Wenxiang; Hu, Xiang; Ci, Suqin; Chen, Junxiang; Wang, Genxiang; Xu, Qiuhua; Wen, Zhenhai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1904054</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although graphite materials have been applied as com. anodes in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), there still remain abundant spaces in the development of carbon-based anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, an electrospinning route is reported to fabricate nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers with interweaved nanochannels (NCNFs-IWNC) that contain robust interconnected 1D porous channels, produced by removal of a Te nanowire template that is coelectrospun within carbon nanofibers during the electrospinning process.  The NCNFs-IWNC features favorable properties, including a conductive 1D interconnected porous structure, a large sp. surface area, expanded interlayer graphite-like spacing, enriched N-doped defects and active sites, toward rapid access and transport of electrolyte and electron/sodium ions.  Systematic electrochem. studies indicate that the NCNFs-IWNC exhibits an impressively high rate capability, delivering a capacity of 148 mA h g-1 at c.d. of as high as 10 A g-1, and has an attractively stable performance over 5000 cycles.  The practical application of the as-designed NCNFs-IWNC for a full SIBs cell is further verified by coupling the NCNFs-IWNC anode with a FeFe(CN)6 cathode, which displays a desirable cycle performance, maintaining acapacity of 97 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3AQQftuUYELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0licY-j9VLnsng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVCmsLfI&amp;md5=6c567dc383582aa700ce9bf659db3e7a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/c7ta08352a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Hollow Porous Carbon Microspheres Derived from Mn-MOFs and Their Electrochemical Behavior for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">23550</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">23558</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D hollow porous carbon microspheres derived from Mn-MOFs and their electrochemical behavior for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Cao, Xiaoyu; Ge, Peng; Zhao, Ganggang; Yin, Dulin; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23550-23558</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Extensive efforts have been put into developing new materials with a 3-dimensional hollow porous spherical structure for increasing their applications in energy storage.  3D hollow porous C microspheres (3DHPCMs) are firstly prepd. by the carbonization and post acid-treatment of 3-dimensional hollow microspherical Mn-MOFs (3DMn-MOFs), showing a high surface area of 788.2 m2 g-1 and a diam. of ∼2 μm.  Importantly, this is the 1st time that the conversion from 1-dimensional nanorods to 3-dimensional hollow spheres of Mn-MOFs through regulating the amt. of poly(vinylpyrrolidone) (PVP) was realized.  Besides, the Na storage behavior of 3-dimensional hollow porous C microspheres is also firstly studied.  When used as anodes for Na ion batteries (SIBs), the 3DHPCMs deliver excellent electrochem. storage performances with a high specific capacity of 313.8 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  Impressively, a high discharge specific capacity of 112.5 mA h g-1 is obtained at 5 A g-1.  The outstanding electrochem. performances can be attributed to the 3-dimensional hollow porous microsphere structure, which can enhance the mech. stability, buffer the vol. expansion, and accelerate the transport of Na+ and electrons.  This work provides a new route for the development of materials with a 3-dimensional hollow spherical structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYNNSCafPDP7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVGQC4ADcV0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yrt7rI&amp;md5=7a4b85da29ff49d1e0e64b4b8d9fb138</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b18834"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Sub-Micro Carbon Fiber@CNTs as Anodes for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Chao; Yuan, Kai; Tian, Te; Bai, Maohui; Wang, Jian-Gan; Li, Xifei; Xie, Keyu; Fu, Qian-Gang; Wei, Bingqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5015-5021</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">K-ion batteries (KIBs) with potential cost benefits are a promising alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs).  However, because of the large radius of K+, current anode materials usually undergo large volumetric expansion and structural collapse during the charge-discharge process.  Self-supporting C nanotubes encapsulated in sub-micro C fiber (SMCF@CNTs) are used as the KIB anode in this study.  The SMCF@CNT anode exhibits high specific capacity, good rate performance, and cycling stability.  The SMCF@CNT electrode has specific capacities of 236 mAh/g at 0.1 C and 108 mAh/g at 5 C and maintains over 193 mAh/g after 300 cycles at 1 C.  A combined capacitive and diffusion-controlled K+ storage mechanism is proposed on the basis of the study using in situ Raman and quant. analyses.  By coupling the SMCF@CNT anode with the K0.3MnO2 cathode, a pouch cell with good flexibility delivers a capacity of 74.0 mAh/g at 20 mA/g.  This work is expected to promote the application of KIBs in wearable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9YNEOKbZp0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVGQC4ADcV0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXkslyjug%253D%253D&amp;md5=50cbfec1968d129b3503222739521aae</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201802074"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yousaf, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, R.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped nanoporous graphitic carbon has attracted great interest because of its distinctive structure and phys. properties.  In this paper, we have proposed a novel method to control Ni-induced graphitization by diffusing Ni nanoparticles from graphitic carbon spheres into N-doped amorphous carbon nanofibers, which turns amorphous carbon into graphitic carbon and produces a hollow-tunnel structure in electrospun carbon/Ni nanofibers.  The resultant materials were further treated by chem. activation and acid treatment to develop activated N-doped hollow-tunneled graphitic carbon nanofibers (ANHTGCNs).  In a typical application, we demonstrate that ANHTGCNs are excellent anode materials for lithium ion batteries (LIBs), displaying a superhigh reversible specific capacity of ∼1560 mA h g-1 and a remarkable volumetric capacity of ∼1.8 A h cm-3 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 with outstanding rate capability and good cycling stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1DcfZzl8zArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVGQC4ADcV0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXht1CltLzK&amp;md5=36b5f4202c040d6a4a89ec627d6e9601</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201700880"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Quan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solvothermal-Derived S-Doped Graphene as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Quan Bo; Jin Longyi; Jin Aihua; Kang Seok Mun; Jeong Juwon; Sung Yung-Eun; Yu Seung-Ho; Abruna Hector D; Piao Yuanzhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted enormous attention in recent years due to the high abundance and low cost of sodium.  However, in contrast to lithium-ion batteries, conventional graphite is unsuitable for SIB anodes because it is much more difficult to intercolate the larger Na ions into graphite layers.  Therefore, it is critical to develop new anode materials for SIBs for practical use.  Here, heteroatom-doped graphene with high doping levels and disordered structures is prepared using a simple and economical thermal process.  The solvothermal-derived graphene shows excellent performance as an anode material for SIBs.  It exhibits a high reversible capacity of 380 mAh g(-1) after 300 cycles at 100 mA g(-1), excellent rate performance 217 mAh g(-1) at 3200 mA g(-1), and superior cycling performance at 2.0 A g(-1) during 1000 cycles with negligible capacity fade.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSgkvoNlgUmKG52AMpI4GK2fW6udTcc2eZAOWrha_fhK7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Scalable synthesis of self-standing sulfur-doped flexible graphene films as recyclable anode materials for low-cost sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Deng, Xiang; Xie, Kongyan; Li, Li; Zhou, Wei; Sunarso, Jaka; Shao, Zongping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The commercialization of anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) requires multitude approaches such as the practicality of the synthesis process, battery performance and the recycling option which most studies overlooked.  Herein, we showed the scalable synthesis of self-standing sulfur-doped flexible graphene films as the anode materials for SIBs, demonstrating up to 377 mA h g-1 capacity at 100 mA g-1 c.d. as well as an excellent rate capability and a moderate decay rate of 0.106% per cycle during long cycling test.  The work also shows that sulfur doping creates addnl. redox sites for reaction with Na+ and induces larger interspacing layers, leading to an enhanced capacity compared to the non-doped graphene.  The self-standing nature of the films also eliminates the need for other addnl. anode components, such as conductive carbon or binder, and more importantly, allows their recovery and subsequent reuse in new applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLOXhnhQjpFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVGQC4ADcV0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XovFWnsbY%253D&amp;md5=e194e91253da06e994049284b2743786</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702409"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Spontaneous Growth of 3D Framework Carbon from Sodium Citrate for High Energy- and Power-Density and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Hybrid Capacitors</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N/S codoped carbon microboxes with expanded interlayer distance toward excellent potassium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Youpeng; Zhong, Wentao; Yang, Chenghao; Zheng, Fenghua; Pan, Qichang; Liu, Yanzhen; Wang, Gang; Xiong, Xunhui; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">358</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are quite attractive for the cost-effective feature.  However, the cycle stability and rate performance of carbonaceous anode materials based on PIBs are limited, for the difficulty of accommodating large K ions (1.38 Å).  Thus, the nitrogen (N) and sulfur (S) codoped carbon microboxes (NSC) with increased interlayer spacing is prepd. via a carbonization-etching process.  Unlike the traditional graphite, in which the K ions are difficult to insert into the restricted interlayer spacing, the NSC displays extremely large interlayer spacing of 0.412 nm, making the K ions more flexible during the insertion/extn. process in NSC.  Moreover, ex-situ TEM study reveals that the layer structure of NSC is well-remained during the potassiation/depotassiation process.  As a result, the NSC delivers super-long cycle life (180.5 mAh/g at 500 mA/g after 1000 cycles) and extraordinary rate ability (155.6 mAh/g at 2 A/g), which makes the NSC a promising anode material for PIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfIH7iaPJnQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQTVLvx2ePOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFKltbrF&amp;md5=859c269a436ae3b518cc45c3dbfbd694</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/d0ee03203d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rao, A.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur-assisted large-scale synthesis of graphene microspheres for superior potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Qingfeng; Cheng, Xueli; Wang, Chengxin; Rao, Apparao M.; Lu, Bingan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">965-974</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-scale low-cost prepn. methods for high quality graphene are crit. for advancing graphene-based applications in energy storage, and beyond.  Here, we present a sulfur-assisted method that converts benzene rings of tetraphenyltin into high purity cryst. graphene.  Specifically, three dimensional few layer graphene microspheres (FLGMs) were prepd. which proved ideal for energy storage applications.  For a potassium ion battery, the FLGM-based anodes exhibited a low discharge platform (av. discharge platform about 0.1 V), a high initial capacity of 285 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1, and a high rate performance (252 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and 95 mA h g-1 at 1000 mA g-1).  Addnl., the FLGM-based anodes exhibited excellent cycling stability with no capacity loss after 1000 cycles at 200 mA g-1.  A process of this nature which does not require substrates, and is scalable for continuous or semi-continuous prodn. of graphene, paves the way for graphene-based energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoKUR53TewtdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQTVLvx2ePOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXis1Wku7rF&amp;md5=edbff6c707c064bf38b3a61e86cea36f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1039/d0ee00477d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Carbon Nanofibers for Compatible Anode and Cathode of Potassium-Ion Hybrid Capacitor</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospinning-Based Strategies for Battery Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xiaoyan; Chen, Weichen; Qian, Qingrong; Huang, Haitao; Chen, Yuming; Wang, Ziqiang; Chen, Qinghua; Yang, Jing; Li, Ju; Mai, Yiu-Wing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electrospinning is a popular technique to prep. 1D tubular/fibrous nanomaterials that assemble into 2D/3D architectures.  When combined with other material processing techniques such as chem. vapor deposition and hydrothermal treatment, electrospinning enables powerful synthesis strategies that can tailor structural and compositional features of energy storage materials.  Herein, a simple description is given of the basic electrospinning technique and its combination with other synthetic approaches.  Then its employment in the prepn. of frameworks and scaffolds with various functions is introduced, e.g., a graphitic tubular network to enhance the electronic cond. and structural integrity of the electrodes.  Current developments in 3D scaffold structures as a host for Li metal anodes, sulfur cathodes, membrane separators, or as a 3D matrix for polymeric solid-state electrolytes for rechargeable batteries are presented.  The use of 1D electrospun nanomaterials as a nanoreactor for in situ transmission electron microscopy (TEM) observations of the mechanisms of materials synthesis and electrochem. reactions is summarized, which has gained popularity due to easy mech. manipulation, electron transparency, electronic cond., and the easy prepositioning of complex chem. ingredients by liq.-soln. processing.  Finally, an outlook on industrial prodn. and future challenges for energy storage materials is given.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1v8CGJAr_xrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQTVLvx2ePOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1WqsrzI&amp;md5=166567bbf391582d4d2a237b3edf601d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/c5ta06844d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, J.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, C.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, I.-D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun Nanofibers as A Platform for Advanced Secondary Batteries: A Comprehensive Review</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun nanofibers as a platform for advanced secondary batteries: a comprehensive review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jung, Ji-Won; Lee, Cho-Long; Yu, Sunmoon; Kim, Il-Doo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Poor electrochem. performances of materials in com. lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) make it difficult to realize battery technologies for future elec. power applications such as energy storage systems and elec. vehicles.  To reach beyond the horizon of state-of-the-art LIBs, the exploration of next generation batteries composed of rationally designed nanomaterials in consideration of the structure, phase and element influencing the battery performance is crit.  By virtue of the simple set-up, versatility, size controllability and mass-productivity of electrospinning, one-dimensional (1D) nanofibers (NFs) produced via electrospinning are attractive candidates for the construction of advanced secondary batteries.  A comprehensive review of the forefront in the development of electrospun NFs as advanced materials of next generation LIBs, sodium-ion batteries (NIBs), lithium-sulfur batteries and lithium-air batteries with particular emphasis on synthesis and improved energy and power d., and cyclability is presented.  In this review, we highlight the recent advancements in electrospun 1D nano-architectures with large surface area to vol. ratios and controllable morphologies as anodes, cathodes, separators, electrolytes and even catalytic materials.  Furthermore, current challenges and prospects of electrospun NFs in both academia and industry are also discussed.  We expect that this review opens up new research activities in a variety of research fields including advanced rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpM-eC08KZwJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOj28Onl5qPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVWmtrzM&amp;md5=75b49725349a6303f43f9166347e8ec7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/c2nr31557b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, Y.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ formation of hollow graphitic carbon nanospheres in electrospun amorphous carbon nanofibers for high-performance Li-based batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Yuming; Lu, Zhouguang; Zhou, Limin; Mai, Yiu-Wing; Huang, Haitao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report on in situ formation of hollow graphitic carbon nanospheres (HGCNs) in amorphous carbon nanofibers (ACNFs) by a combination of electrospinning, calcination and acid treatment.  The prepd. carbon nanofibers contain many HGCNs on which defects such as discontinuous graphene sheets with a large d-spacing in their wall exist and provide extra sites for Li+ storage and serve as buffers for withstanding large vol. expansion and shrinkage during the Li insertion and extn. procedure.  Furthermore, some exposed HGCNs on the surface of the ACNFs as well as hollow structures are favorable for lithium ion diffusion from different orientations and sufficient contact between active material and electrolyte.  In addn., the high cond. architectures facilitate collection and transport of electrons during the cycling process.  As a result, the ACNFs/HGCNs display a high reversible specific gravimetric capacity of ∼750 mA h g-1 and volumetric capacity of ∼1.1 A h cm-3 with outstanding rate capability and good cycling stability, which is superior to those of carbon nanofibers (CNFs), carbon nanotubes (CNTs), porous ACNFs, graphene nanosheets (GNSs), GNSs/CNFs, hollow carbon nanospheres and graphite.  The synthesis process is simple, low-cost and environmentally friendly, providing new avenues for the rational engineering of high-energy carbon-based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo8rd5wBE8zV7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOj28Onl5qPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsV2qs73E&amp;md5=2b9d26e6fd9eab9926986e11b56b16a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2021.02.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rational Design of Microstructure and Interphase Nnables High-Capacity and Long-Life Carbon Anodes for Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>176</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">383</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">389</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design of microstructure and interphase enables high-capacity and long-life carbon anodes for potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tan, Hong; Du, Xiaoqiong; Zhou, Rui; Hou, Zhen; Zhang, Biao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">176</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">383-389</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Disordered carbon is considered as a potential anode material for potassium ion batteries (PIBs) due to its advantages in rate capability compared to graphite.  Nevertheless, its capacity is usually limited below 300 mAh g-1.  Herein, we demonstrate the performance of low-cost pitch derived carbon could be significantly boosted through synergistic microstructure design and electrode/electrolyte interphase regulation.  A considerable amt. of mesopores are produced to provide the extra active sites for K ion storage and meanwhile, facilitate the charge transfer.  The optimized carbon anode delivers a remarkable capacity of 460 mAh g-1 with outstanding rate capability up to 4.0 A g-1.  In-situ Raman spectra reveal the superb performance originates from K ion storage in both the mesopore and disordered graphene layers.  The construction of a robust solid electrolyte interphase in ethylene glycol di-Et ether derived electrolyte further improves the long-term stability, leading to an exceptional capacity retention of 80% after 2000 cycles under a c.d. of 1.0 A g-1.  This strategy provides a facile approach to enhance the performance of carbon materials for PIBs via structure and interphase design.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqO53d0t4Ib47Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOj28Onl5qPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktVOjsbk%253D&amp;md5=e15a23cc62342a39f802d4cb75ce30e5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1039/c7gc01942d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation of S/N-Codoped Carbon Nanosheets with Tunable Interlayer Distance for High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Green Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4622</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4632</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of S/N-codoped carbon nanosheets with tunable interlayer distance for high-rate sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Zhao, Ganggang; Huang, Zhaodong; Ge, Peng; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Green Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4622-4632</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">GRCHFJ</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The conventional strategies for obtaining S/N-codoped carbon materials suffer from a series of problems caused by their complicated exptl. procedures.  Here, S,N-codoped carbon nanosheets were firstly prepd. by a solvent-free one-pot method, displaying an ultra-thin sheet-like structure, a tunable interlayer distance ranging from 0.37 nm to 0.41 nm, and a large surface area up to 809 m2 g-1.  When they were used as an anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), an outstanding sodium-ion storage performance of 380 mA h g-1 was acquired at 100 mA g-1, which can be attributed to the expanded interlayer distance caused by the introduction of the large covalent radius-sulfur.  The initial coulombic efficiency improved to 60.9%, which may benefit from N-doping.  Most importantly, an excellent rate capability of ∼178 mA h g-1 was obsd. at a c.d. of 5 A g-1 after 5000 cycles, which is among best of the state-of-the-art carbon-based SIBs.  Interestingly, the morphol. of the obtained carbon materials can be tuned from bulk to flake by adjusting the sulfur content or temp.  Given this, this work provides a new method to construct co-doped carbon (esp. tri-doped and multi-doped carbon) and shows that the strategy of co-doping of heteroatoms can effectively optimize the nano/microstructure and enhance the rate capability of the carbon materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3XQf2smg2BbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOj28Onl5qPQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and Sulfur Co-Doped Graphene Nanosheets to Improve Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xiangdong; Zeng, Hongliang; Han, Dezhi; Qiao, Ke; Xing, Wei; Rood, Mark J.; Yan, Zifeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">37172-37180</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) attract more attention because of sodium's abundant availability, affordable price, and potential to be an effective anode material.  Meanwhile, carbon-based materials provide the most promising anode materials.  Because of the large radius of sodium ions, SIBs do not exhibit favorable electrochem. performance.  Introducing heteroatoms into the carbon-lattice is an effective strategy to enlarge the interlayer space of carbon-based materials which can improve carbon's electrochem. performance.  In addn., anode materials with a surface-induced capacitive process can enhance the SIB's electrochem. performance because its capacitive process increases the kinetics of ion diffusion.  Here, we describe an SIB's anode material contg. nitrogen and sulfur co-doped graphene sheets [denoted as poly(2,5-dimercapto-1,3,4-thiadiazole) (PDMcT)/reduced graphene oxide (RGO)] which are synthesized via carbonization of PDMcT polymd. on the surface of GO.  PDMcT/RGO exhibited high capacities (240 mA h g-1 at 500 mA g-1), improved rate performance (144 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1), and good cycling stability (153 mA h g-1 after 5000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1).  These unique results are attributed to the enlarged interlayer spacing and electronic cond. from the heteroatoms which facilitate the sodium ion's insertion and electron transport.  These results represent that PDMcT/RGO is a great potential anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGopriUKV_hK67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOj28Onl5qPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVKlurrN&amp;md5=195429390d2051ea31a9758b9317031c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202101576"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, Y.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A new strategy for achieving high K+ storage capacity with fast kinetics: realizing covalent sulfur-rich carbon by phosphorous doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Wenrui; Zheng, Yulong; Huang, Minghua; Shi, Jing; Li, Lei; Shi, Zhicheng; Liu, Shuai; Wang, Huanlei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing carbon anodes with rich heteroatoms and dilated graphitic interlayer spacing via a one-step synthesis process plays a vital role in accelerating the practical application of potassium ion batteries, but it is still a big challenge.  Herein, P-doped S-rich mesoporous carbon (PSMC) is prepd. by direct phosphate-assisted carbonization of carrageenan, and it exhibits excellent potassium storage capacity (449 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), superior rate performance (233 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1) and long-term stability (97.3% capacity retention after 1000 cycles), due to the high sulfur doping (16.48 wt%) and the coexistence of ordered and disordered regions in the structure.  Ex situ characterization, GITT and theor. calcns. reveal that the promotion of covalent sulfur can effectively increase the adsorption of K+ and enhance the K+ reaction kinetics. We consider one, two and three impurity atoms by substitution on the graphene and obtain doping formation energies of 5.78, 7.43 and 10.53 eV for sulfur impurities and 2.73, 0.54 and 1.82 eV for phosphorous impurities.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Functionalized Carbon Surface for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Qiaowei; Zhang, Jun; Lv, Wei; Ma, Jiabin; He, Yanbing; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are promising for large-scale energy storage systems and carbon materials are the most likely candidates for their electrodes.  The existence of defects in carbon materials is crucial for increasing the sodium storage ability.  However, both the reversible capacity and efficiency need to be further improved.  Functionalization is a direct and feasible approach to address this issue.  Based on the structural changes in carbon materials produced by surface functionalization, three basic categories are defined: heteroatom doping, grafting of functional groups, and the shielding of defects.  Heteroatom doping can improve the electrochem. reactivity, and the grafting of functional groups can promote both the diffusion-controlled bulk process and surface-confined capacitive process.  The shielding of defects can further increase the efficiency and cyclic stability without sacrificing reversible capacity.  In this review, recent progresses in the ways to produce surface functionalization are presented and the related impact on the phys. and chem. properties of carbon materials is discussed.  Moreover, the crit. issues, challenges, and possibilities for future research are summarized.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMEHLH9L1xnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgSsyZYdDAYSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsFChs7rN&amp;md5=e95d85881a59a547d9d2c2a40b531efb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131032"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stabilizing Plasma-Induced Highly Nitrogen-Deficient g-C3N4 by Heteroatom-Refilling for Excellent Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stabilizing plasma-induced highly nitrogen-deficient g-C3N4 by heteroatom-refilling for excellent lithium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Shangqi; Wu, Youchun; Zhu, Jianfeng; Lu, Chengjie; Sun, Yang; Wang, Zhen; Chen, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The modulation of vacancies is an attractive strategy to improve the conductivities of semiconductor materials for high-performance electrodes in lithium-ion batteries.  However, it is a dilemma that the defective structure with high content vacancies is instable and also hard to preserve during long-term cycling.  Herein, a heteroatom-refilling strategy has been proposed with the example of refilling oxygen in nitrogen-deficient g-C3N4.  With the support of theoretic prediction, we produced the g-C3N4 with high nitrogen vacancies (C/N ∼ 2.52) by high-energy hydrogen plasma bombardment, and then filled oxygen by exposure to air.  The obtained oxygen refilled g-C3N4 shows not only improved cond. but also superior electrochem. performance (high capacity of 647 mAh·g-1 after 400 cycles at 0.1 A·g-1 and ultra-stable cycle of 232.8 mAh·g-1 after 5000 cycles at 1 A·g-1).  It is found that such enhancement is contributed by the reduced band gap, enhanced lithium absorption energy and different charge d. due to the vacancy modulation as well as the increased sp. surface and active sites caused by the plasma bombardment.  Our work proves the vacancy modulation strategy with heteroatom-refilling and the tech. approach of the plasma-based method are effective and have abroad applications in energy and other fields.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGooIEEcINL45rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgSsyZYdDAYSw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-ion capacitors (LICs) are a relatively new hybrid systems that combine the merits of Faradaic and capacitive behaviors, demonstrating great potentials in modern applications.  However, the mismatch in reaction kinetics between these two types of electrode materials, the slow Faradaic reaction in the battery anode and the rapid adsorption/desorption process in the capacitor cathode, severely restricts the application of LICs.  In this study, the porous yolk-shell selenide frameworks (ZnSe@CoSe2) are constructed using the core-shell ZIF-8@ZIF-67 as precursor by a sequential thermal program.  Detailed morphol. investigation discloses that the yolk-shell structure is in-situ formed during the early incubation at lower temp.  The yolk-shell ZnSe@CoSe2 frameworks in an N-doping carbon layer (Z@C@P) as the anode material for lithium-ion batteries, which exhibits high rate capability and good cycle stability at a high c.d. of 2 A/g, which greatly bridges the kinetic gap with the capacitor-type electrode.  Thereby, the assembled LICs with active carbon show high energy d., power d. and capacity retention rate.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible Na/K-ion batteries (NIBs/KIBs) exhibit great potential applications and have drawn much attention due to the continuous development of flexible electronics.  However, there are still many huge challenges, mainly the design and construction of flexible electrodes (cathode and anode) with outstanding electrochem. properties.  In this work, a unique approach to prep. flexible electrode is proposed by utilizing the com. available cotton cloth-derived carbon cloth (CC) as a flexible anode and the substrate of a cathode.  The binder-free, self-supporting, and flexible cathodes (FCC@N/KPB) are prepd. by growing Prussian blue microcubes on the flexible CC (FCC).  Na/K-ion full batteries (FCC//FCC@N/KPB) are assembled by using FCC and FCC@N/KPB as anode and cathode, resp.  Electrochem. performance, mech. flexibility, and practicability of FCC//FCC@N/KPB Na/K-ion full batteries are evaluated in both coin cells and flexible pouch cells, demonstrating their superior energy-storage properties (excellent rate performance and cycling stability) and remarkable flexibility (they can work under different bending states).  This work provides a new and profound strategy to design flexible electrodes, promoting the development of flexible NIBs/KIBs to be practical and sustainable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoc0z13bQu63rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh0kI-hRcjkcg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs1emsbvN&amp;md5=2820dfe489efe15e0835b400ba8c709e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703159"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting Fast Sodium Storage of a Large-Scalable Carbon Anode with an Ultralong Cycle Life</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Designing and Understanding the Superior Potassium Storage Performance of Nitrogen/Phosphorus Co-Doped Hollow Porous Bowl-Like Carbon Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Jiamin; Cheng, Yong; Zhang, Qiaobao; Luo, Chong; Li, Hong-Yang; Wu, Ying; Zhang, Hehe; Wang, Xiang; Liu, Haodong; He, Xin; Han, Jiajia; Peng, Dong-Liang; Liu, Meilin; Wang, Ming-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2007158</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries because of the advantage of abundant, low-cost potassium resources.  However, PIBs are facing a pivotal challenge to develop suitable electrode materials for efficient insertion/extn. of large-radius potassium ions (K+).  Here, a viable anode material composed of uniform, hollow porous bowl-like hard carbon dual doped with nitrogen (N) and phosphorus (P) (denoted as N/P-HPCB) is developed for high-performance PIBs.  With prominent merits in structure, the as-fabricated N/P-HPCB electrode manifests extraordinary potassium storage performance in terms of high reversible capacity (458.3 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1), superior rate performance (213.6 mAh g-1 at 4 A g-1), and long-term cyclability (205.2 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 2 A g-1).  D.-functional theory calcns. reveal the merits of N/P dual doping in favor of facilitating the adsorption/diffusion of K+ and enhancing the electronic cond., guaranteeing improved capacity, and rate capability.  Moreover, in situ transmission electron microscopy in conjunction with ex situ microscopy and Raman spectroscopy confirms the exceptional cycling stability originating from the excellent phase reversibility and robust structure integrity of N/P-HPCB electrode during cycling.  Overall, the findings shed light on the development of high-performance, durable carbon anodes for advanced PIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVW_BflakEhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh0kI-hRcjkcg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitlemtr7I&amp;md5=c33389ca96e84b4394de35107ad03d4a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201901533"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast Redox Kinetics in Bi-Heteroatom Doped 3D Porous Carbon Nanosheets for High-Performance Hybrid Potassium-Ion Battery Capacitors</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1901533</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fast Redox Kinetics in Bi-Heteroatom Doped 3D Porous Carbon Nanosheets for High-Performance Hybrid Potassium-Ion Battery Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Xiang; Liu, Yangjie; Chen, Junxiang; Yi, Luocai; Zhan, Hongbing; Wen, Zhenhai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1901533</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion hybrid capacitors (PIHCs) hold the advantages of high-energy d. of batteries and high-power output of supercapacitors and thus present great promise for the next generation of electrochem. energy storage devices.  One of the most crucial tasks for developing a high-performance PIHCs is to explore a favorable anode material with capability to balance the kinetics mismatch between battery-type anodes and capacitor-type cathode.  Herein, a reliable route for fabricating sulfur and nitrogen codoped 3D porous carbon nanosheets (S-N-PCNs) is reported.  Systematic characterizations coupled with kinetics anal. indicate that the doped heteroatoms of sulfur and nitrogen and the amplified graphite interlayer can provide ample structural deffects and redox active sites that are beneficial for improving pseudocapacitive activity, enabling fast kinetics toward efficient potassium-ion storage.  The S-N-PCNs are demonstrated to exhibit superior potassium storage capability with a high capacity of 107 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1 and long cycle stability.  The as-developed PIHCs present impressive electrochem. performance with an operating voltage as high as 4.0 V, an energy d. of 187 Wh kg-1, a power d. of 5136 W kg-1, and a capacity retention of 86.4% after 3000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3UGZvnKyMsrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh0kI-hRcjkcg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhslyitLzL&amp;md5=ed84e02c7b0dd1546a8099ba86cd8525</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2019.03.143"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sulfur and Nitrogen Dual-Doped Porous Carbon Nanosheet Anode for Sodium Ion Storage with A Self-Template and Self-Porogen Method</span>. <i>Appl.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulfur and nitrogen dual-doped porous carbon nanosheet anode for sodium ion storage with a self-template and self-porogen method</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Qian; Meng, Yan; Li, Jing; Xiao, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The porous carbon nanosheets (as thin as 8 nm) doped with sulfur and nitrogen have been synthesized by directly carbonizing laminaria japonica with a self-template and self-porogen method.  Laminaria japonica contains plenty of sodium chloride and potassium compds., which can be a natural template and the natural porogen, resp.  The obtained carbons possess a three-dimensional connected nanosheet structure with a large sp. surface area of 1900 m2 g-1, a total pore vol. of 1.04 cm3 g-1, a pore size distribution centering mainly at around 1.4 nm and 2.7 nm, a S-content of 9.12% and a N-content of 4.52%.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly nitrogen doped carbon nanofibers with superior rate capability and cyclability for potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Yang; Zhou Min; Lei Yong; Zhang Chenglin; Fu Qun; Wu Minghong; Zhao Chengxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1720</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries are a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  However, it is challenging to achieve fast charging/discharging and long cycle life with the current electrode materials because of the sluggish potassiation kinetics.  Here we report a soft carbon anode, namely highly nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers, with superior rate capability and cyclability.  The anode delivers reversible capacities of 248 mAh g(-1) at 25 mA g(-1) and 101 mAh g(-1) at 20 A g(-1), and retains 146 mAh g(-1) at 2 A g(-1) after 4000 cycles.  Surface-dominated K-storage is verified by quantitative kinetics analysis and theoretical investigation.  A full cell coupling the anode and Prussian blue cathode delivers a reversible capacity of 195 mAh g(-1) at 0.2 A g(-1).  Considering the cost-effectiveness and material sustainability, our work may shed some light on searching for K-storage materials with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSJFZPVkzYHGDUE-swuRqsHfW6udTcc2ebqsm5P7R2Ry7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1MjosVCmsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=72421c9e5cc7c2c9892fb5f83f22dcb1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201800241"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Foster, C.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced Hierarchical Vesicular Carbon Co-Doped with S, P, N for High-Rate Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou Guoqiang; Hou Hongshuai; Guo Tianxiao; Jiang Yunling; Ji Xiaobo; Zou Guoqiang; Hou Hongshuai; Guo Tianxiao; Jiang Yunling; Ji Xiaobo; Foster Christopher W; Banks Craig E; Zhang Yun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1800241</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical nanoscale carbons have received wide interest as electrode materials for energy storage and conversion due to their fast mass transfer processes, outstanding electronic conductivity, and high stability.  Here, heteroatom (S, P, and N) doped hierarchical vesicular carbon (HHVC) materials with a high surface area up to 867.5 m(2) g(-1) are successfully prepared using a surface polymerization of hexachloro-cyclotriphosphazene (HCCP) and 4,4'-sulfonyldiphenol (BPS) on the ZIF-8 polyhedrons.  Significantly, it is the first time to achieve a controllability of the wall thickness for this unique carbon, ranging from 18 to 52 nm.  When utilized as anodes for sodium ion batteries, these novel carbon materials exhibit a high specific capacity of 327.2 mAh g(-1) at 100 mA g(-1) after 100 cycles, which can be attributed to the expanded interlayer distance and enhanced conductivity derived from the doping of heteroatoms.  Importantly, a high capacity of 142.6 mAh g(-1) can be obtained even at a high current density of 5 A g(-1), assigning to fast ion/electronic transmission processes stemming from the unique hierarchical vesicular structure.  This work offers a new route for the fabrication/preparation of multi-heteroatom doped hierarchical vesicular materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQhfPEft8OQvP69nzq6467DfW6udTcc2ebqsm5P7R2Ry7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3c7gtVKqug%253D%253D&amp;md5=ed89c2798a7d203205fb2a79ba3088c2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201701648"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Short-Range Order in Mesoporous Carbon Boosts Potassium-Ion Battery Performance</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/aenm.201701648</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D1701648%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DW.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BZhao%26author%3DP.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DH.%2BHuang%26author%3DS.%2BGuo%26title%3DShort-Range%2BOrder%2Bin%2BMesoporous%2BCarbon%2BBoosts%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBattery%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201701648&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c12470&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201701648&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52');
